Jamison Brereton

38 (334)
Heaven and Earth (1), Dadhikra╠Д (2тАУ10)
V─Бmadeva Gautama
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn and the next two (IV.39тАУ40) are dedicated to a horse known as Dadhikr─Б(van), a prizewinning racer and a warhorse. Although no doubt in part referring to a real horse belonging to Trasadasyu, king of the P┼лrus, it also repre sents the sacrificial horse of the great royal sacrifice, the A┼Ыvamedha, and a symbol of P┼лru, and then general ─Аrya, hegemony. In this capacity it is compared to the sun, in the last, triumphal verse.
What the reader will notice most, however, is the exuberance and precision of the equine imagery, emphasizing especially the headlong speed of the horse and his constant goal: groups of female animals, presumably mares. The sense of speed is enhanced by the regular use of тАЬandтАЭ to string verses together; indeed, the hymn begins with one. Unfortunately some of the imagery is not entirely clear; see espe
cially verse 4, where some of the translation is provisional.

Although the Anukramaс╣З─л assigns the first verse to Heaven and Earth, it is more likely that Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are the referents of the unspecified duals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Dadhikr─Б The middle vss. of this hymn are introduced by repeated ut├б sma (5, 6, 8, 9), varied by ut├б sy├б in 7. As noted in the published introduction, this sequence of тАШandтАЩs adds to the sense of speed.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTrasadasyu has bestowed upon many the ancient (gifts) which were obtained by the liberal (prince) through your (favour, Heaven and Earth) you two have given a horse, a son, a weapon (for the destruction) of the Dasyus, fierce and foe-subduing.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Heaven and earth: the dual pronoun, v─Бm, of you two, implies heaven and earth; you two have given a horse, a son: kс╣гetr─Бs─Бm : from kс╣гetra, land;

Urvar─Бs─Бm: urvara, fertile soil;

San = to give

Jamison Brereton

And since the earlier gifts were from you two [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa], the ones that Trasadasyu was to send spilling down for the P┼лrus,
you have (also) given the one [=horse] who wins dwelling places, who wins meadows, a bane for the Dasyus, overwhelming, powerful.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the Anukramaс╣З─л takes Heaven and Earth to be the deity of this vs., the unidentified duals must rather refer to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, as also in vs. 2. This is clear from IV.39, where Mitra and Varuс╣Зa give Dadhikr─Б to the Purus (2cd, 5cd).

The published translation doesnтАЩt accurately reflect s├бnti in p─Бda a. The tr. should read тАЬSince there are earlier gifts тАжтАЭ The form nito┼Ы├й is much disputed. Grassmann identifies it as a 3rd sg. to the thematic pres. to┼Ыate (otherwise unaccented), but not only is there a perfectly fine -te 3rd sg.

(to┼Ыate 4x) while a t-less 3rd sg. would be anomalous, but given the full-grade we would expect root accent (*nit├│┼Ыe). Oldenberg vacillates but displays a weak preference for a 3rd sg. unreduplicated perfect, and Geldner, who does not comment, appears to follow him (тАЬтАж ausgesch├╝ttet hatтАЭ). Despite this scholarly pedigree, this solution appears to me to have little to recommend it: non-reduplicated perfects are quite rare. Got┼Н (1st Kl, 167-68) also vacillates: if itтАЩs a verb itтАЩs a non-redupl. pf. Or it might be the loc. of a noun nito┼Ы├б-; this appears to be the view represented in Witzel Got┼Н. There does exist a them. noun to┼Ы├б-. Renou also tentatively suggests a locative but тАЬ├а nuance semiinfinitive,тАЭ tr. тАЬpour ├кtre d├йvers├йes.тАЭ I find RenouтАЩs interpr. appealing, though, as often, somewhat cavalier about grammar. I would like to take the form directly as a dative root noun in infinitival usage, but we should probably expect *nitu┼Ы├й. It may have been adjusted to match the grade of to┼Ы├б-, or the loc. ending -├й of the them. noun may have been reinterpr. as a purpose dative. One might expect the hapax naito┼Ы├б- to provide some help, but it is only found in the impenetrable A┼Ыvin hymn X.106.6, which appears to be written in code. In any event, the point of the hemistich seems to be that Mitra and Varuс╣Зa provided gifts to Trasadasyu, who then redistributed them to his subjects the Purus in an appropriately kingly way.

Griffith

FROM you two came the gifts in days aforetime which Trasadasyu granted to the Purus.
Ye gave the winner of our fields and plough-lands, and the strong smiter who subdued the Dasytis.

Geldner

Von euch stammen ja auch die fr├╝heren Gaben, die Trasadasyu ├╝ber die Puru┬┤s ausgesch├╝ttet hat. Ihr beide habt den landgewinnenden, feldgewinnenden Trasadasyu geschenkt, den Hammer f├╝r die Dasyu┬┤s, den ├╝berlegenen, gewaltigen.

Grassmann

Ihr beide gabt ja einst die alten Gaben, die Trasadasju dann verlieh den Menschen, Ihr gabet den, der Fluren schenkt und Felder, den Feindetilger, den gewalt’gen Sieger.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd you two have given the swift Dadhikr─Б, the repeller of many (foes), the defender of all men, the straight-going, the graceful-moving, the resplendent, the rapid, the destroyer of enemies like a heroic prince.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dadhikr─Б: dadhikr─Бvan, synonym of a┼Ыva, a horse;

Derivation: from, dadhi, who bears, who carries his rider; krama, to go

Jamison Brereton

And a prizewinner providing many fulfillments have you givenтАФ Dadhikr─Б, who belongs to all the communities,
a straight-flying falcon, frothing at the mouth, swift, to be constantly celebrated by the stranger, a champion like a lord of men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On -niс╣гс╣г├нdh- see comm. ad III.51.5. It is possible here that -niс╣гс╣г├нdh- тАШtributesтАЩ are owed to Dadhikr─Б rather than provided by him. Cf. Klein (DGRV I.420) тАЬto whom many tributes are dueтАЭ; this would fit better with carkс╣Ы╠Бtyam ary├бс╕е.

For pruс╣гita-psu- тАШfrothing at the mouthтАЩ (тЖР тАШhaving spraying breathтАЩ), see EWA s.v. psu-.

Griffith

And ye gave mighty Dadhikras, the giver of many gifts, who visiteth all people,
Impetuous hawk, swift and of varied colour, like a brave King whom each true man must honour.

Geldner

Und ihr habt das Siegerro├Я Dadhikra gegeben, dem man viel verdankt, den in allen L├дndern bekannten, den wie der Adler dahinschie├Яenden, fleckfarbigen Renner, der f├╝r den hohen Herrn des Andenkens w├╝rdig, tapfer wie der K├╢nig ist.

Grassmann

Ihr gabt das Ross, das viele Gaben spendet, den Dadhikra, der allen Menschen zukommt, Den schnellen bunten Adler, der dahinschiesst, als preisenswerther Held, ein F├╝rst des Treuen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhom all men, rejoicing, praise, rushing everywhere, as if down a precipice, springing with his feet like a hero eager for war, drawing a car, and going as swift as the wind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The one whom every P┼лru applauds in excitement as he runs as if down an easy slopeтАФ
greedy with his hooves like a champion seeking his meal, outstripping chariots, swooping like the wind.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is sharp difference of opinion about the sense of medhay├║-: is it built to medh─Б╠Б- тАШwisdomтАЩ or m├йdha- тАШritual offering, mealтАЩ? The former is the choice of Geldner, Renou, Mayr (tentatively, EWA, s.v. medh─Б╠Б-), while Grassmann, Scarlatta (188), and I opt for тАШmealтАЩ. (Witzel Got┼НтАЩs rendering тАЬwie ein Opfertier VerlangenderтАЭ must also reflect this m├йdha- stem.) The тАШmealтАЩ interpr. fits well with gс╣Ы╠Бdhyantam тАШgreedyтАЩ, and it also makes more sense to me that a horse would want something to eat rather than wisdom. Moreover, if Dadhikr─Б represents the sacrificial horse in the A┼Ыvamedha, there is a (sinister) echo of the name of this sacrifice: the horse is unwittingly seeking his own sacrifice. It can, of course, also be a pun.

Griffith

Whom, as ’twere down a precipice, swift rushing, each Puru praises and his heart rejoices,-
Springing forth like a hero fain for battle, whirling the car and flying like the tempest.

Dem, wenn er l├дuft gleichwie im j├дhen Sturze, ein jeder Mensch erfreut entgegen jubelt; Im Laufe strebt er, wie ein Held nach Beute, den Wagen f├╢rdernd, fliegend wie der Sturmwind.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho, opposing the mingled multitude in battles, rushes eager, passing through the regions, whose vigour is manifestl, who, understanding what is to be known, puts to shame the adversary of the (pious) man.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vidhat─Б nicikyat tiro aratim pary─Бpa ─Бyoс╕е = j├▒─Бtavy─Бni janam araman─Бm arim v─Б tiraskaroti stoturmanuс╣гyasya, knowing things cognizable, who disgraces the opponent, or the foe of the man, the praiser

Jamison Brereton

The one who, hemming in the things to be seized in battles, keeps going to (the contests for) cows as one better at winning,
foaming visibly, setting his attention on the (rites of) distribution,
across the circlet (of fire? the sun?), around the waters of ─Аyu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains a number of puzzles, though the general purport – the success of Dadhikr─Б in battles and raids – is clear.

g├бdhya- elsewhere (3x) modifies v─Б╠Бja- тАШprizeтАЩ, but that precise word canтАЩt be supplied here, because it is masc. and g├бdhy─Б must be neut. pl. Nonetheless, battle spoils or the like must be meant. GeldnerтАЩs rendering of g├бdhya- as тАЬbis an die Wagendecke reichende (Beute)тАЭ must rest on the later (s┼лtra) gadh─Б тАШVerdeck des LastwagensтАЩ (see EWA s.v.), but given the chronological gap and the fact that EWA considers the etym. of gadh─Б unklar, this seems unnecessary. Geldner is consistent: the other occurrences of g├бdhya- he tr. тАШdeckenhoheтАЩ.

I take c├бrati тАж g├бchan as a periphrasis, тАЬkeeps going,тАЭ though the standard tr.

take the two verbal forms separately. There is no way to tell. The problematic form in this p─Бda is s├бnutaraс╕е, about which there is no consensus even on what part of speech it represents. The uncertainty can be seen acutely in MayrhoferтАЩs changing approach to it. In KEWA (s.v. sanut├бс╕е) he tentatively decides to follow AiG II.2.596, 608, 698 in taking it as a comparative built to the verb stem san├│ti, meaning тАШmehr gewinnendтАЩ (an interpr. that goes back, one way or the other, to S─Бyaс╣Зa.). But in EWA (s.v. sanut├бr) he has changed his mind, attaching it rather to the adv. sanut├бr тАШawayтАЩ, attributing its aberrant form to reinterpretation by this late poet, and citing Tichy (Nom. agen. 58-59), who suggests itтАЩs a comparative to the adv. Both Geldner and Renou derive it from тИЪsan тАШwinтАЩ, though in different ways: GeldnerтАЩs tr. (тАЬals bester GewinnerтАЭ) seems to reflect the comparative interpr. favored by S─Бyaс╣Зa. and AiG (though transposed into the superlative); Renou (тАЬgagnantтАЭ) explicitly suggests that it stands for *s├бnutra-, formed like t├бrutra-, an interpr. that Grassmann also gestures towards. Oldenberg favors a connection with the adv. sanut├бr, as do Witzel Got┼Н (flg. Tichy), tr. тАЬimmer ferner wandelt.тАЭ My tr. reflects an analysis as comparative agent noun to тИЪsan (тАЬas one better at winningтАЭ), but I do not feel strongly about it. In fact, I would probably now emend my tr. to тАЬkeeps going further in (the contests for) cowsтАЭ: the contrast between his hemming in the booty in a and himself going further in b would be thematically nice, and if I am correct about the meaning of d, the expansion of the horseтАЩs wanderings further and further would be appropriate to what is expressed in d. But I am not certain that this question can be decided.

My interpr. of ─Бv├нrс╣Ыj─лkaс╕е rests on ThiemeтАЩs (Unt. p. 40, n. 2): ‘an dem der Schaum hervortrittтАЩ. This image responds to pruс╣гit├бpsum in 2c.

vid├бth─Б nic├нkyat recurs in AV V.20.12.

The last p─Бda is the most baffling of all. The second part of it, p├бry ─Б╠Бpa ─Бy├│с╕е, is also found at I.178.1 (q.v.). The major question is the identity of ─Б╠Бpaс╕е: is it a form of тИЪ─Бp тАШreach, acquireтАЩ, whether verbal or nominal (so Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н); is it a derivative of ├бpas- тАШworkтАЩ (so Grassmann, Renou; dubious EWA s.v. ├бpas-); or is it the nom. pl. of ├бp- тАШwaterтАЩ, used as an acc. (Oldenberg, Thieme, Witzel Got┼Н possibly [in n.])? I follow ThiemeтАЩs interpr.

(Unters. 40-41), which sees тАЬthe waters of ─АyuтАЭ as an expression referring to land habitable because it is well watered. If this phrase is essentially locational, then one might expect the preceding tir├│ arat├нm to be as well: тАЬacross the arat├н-.тАЭ Unfortunately, though ThiemeтАЩs general interpr. of arat├н- I find persuasive, his tr. of this phrase тАЬschneller als die R├дder [seines Wagens]тАЭ is problematic, because I do not see how tir├бс╕е can mean тАШfasterтАЩ. It is always otherwise a preposition/adverb. I therefore think Dadhikr─Б is being depicted as crossing the arat├н and racing around тАЬthe waters of ─Аyu.тАЭ These two locational phrases may refer to the ritual ground, as Oldenberg suggests: the horse runs across the fire on the ritual ground and around the water vessels used for the sacrifice. Or, my preference, it can refer to the territory of the ─Аrya, which the horse traverses and thus, as it were, claims for his owner (much as the A┼Ыvamedha horse does in his year-long pre-sacificial ramble). What arat├н- would stand for in this scenario isnтАЩt entirely clear to me – but since arat├н- can mean тАШspoked wheel, circlet, circleтАЩ, I would tentatively suggest that the horse runs across a notional circle of land belonging to / claimed by / aspired to by the ─Аrya and then around the periphery of this circle to enclose it as ─Аrya possession. I would therefore now emend my tr. to тАЬacross the circle (of ─Аrya land), around the waters of ─Аyu.тАЭ

Griffith

Who gaineth precious booty in the combats and moveth, winning spoil, among the cattle;
Shown in bright colour, looking on the assemblies, beyond the churl, to worship of the living.

Geldner

Der in den K├дmpfen bis an die Wagendecke reichende Beute errafft, der als bester Gewinner hervorgeht, wenn er auf Rinder auszieht, seine Vorz├╝ge offenbarend, die weisen Worte verstehend, seinen Lenker noch ├╝bertreffend, mehr als Ayu zu erreichen vermag.

Grassmann

Der an sich reisst die Beute in den Schlachten, der Gut gewinnt, der eilt, nach K├╝hen strebend, Den Trank erblickend und die Opfer schauend, vorbei am B├╢sen zu dem Werk des Frommen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhom men call after in battles, as after a thief carrying off a garment, or as (after) a hungry hawk pouncing (upon his prey); they call after him, hastening to obtain food, or a herd of cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They call after him: ┼Ыravasc─Бcch─Б pa┼Ыumacca y┼лtham = annam k─лrttim v─Б pa┼Ыumad y┼лtham ca acch─Б abhilakс╣гya gacchantam enam anukro┼Ыanti, they call after him, that is Dadhikr─Б, going, having in view either food or fame, or a herd consisting of cattle

Jamison Brereton

And the settled peoples shriek after him at his raidings as if after a thief who steals clothes,
as he makes his way downward like a famished falcon toward fame and a herd full of livestock.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme ├бnu тИЪkru┼Ы is later a semi-technical term for raising the hue-andcry, which would be appropriate in this context.

There is a phonological echo of 4c nic├нkyat in 5c n─лc─Б╠Бyam─Бnam, although the latter is to be analyzed as n─лc─Б╠Б+├бyam─Бnam. The latter belongs to the marginal thematized pres. ├бyate to тИЪi (see Got┼Н, 1st Kl., 92-97). There is one other occurrence of this medial part. in the RV, otherwise a few finite forms, some of which are ambiguous between subjunctive to the root pres. and indicative to a them. pres.

Griffith

Loudly the folk cry after him in battles, as ’twere a thief who steals away a garment;
Speeding to glory, or a herd of cattle, even as a hungry falcon swooping downward.

Geldner

Und die V├╢lker schreien ihm in den K├дmpfen nach wie einem Dieb, der Kleider raubt, wenn er wie ein niedersto├Яender hungriger Adler auf den Ruhmespreis und auf die Viehherde losst├╝rmt.

Grassmann

Ihm schreien nach die Feinde in den Schlachten, wie einem Diebe, der das Kleid geraubt hat, Wie einem Adler, der voll Gier herabf├дhrt auf sch├╢nes Gut und rinderreiche Heerde.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd who, issuing forth the first in those encounters, rushes in various directions with rows of chariots; like an elegant (courser), friendly to man, decorated with a garland, raising the dust, and champing his bit.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And desiring to run first, he keeps bearing down upon them (fem. [=mares?]), with the ranks of chariots,
garlanding himself like a resplendent groomsman, constantly licking the dust, having bitten the grit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referent and construction of ─Бsu require discussion. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) construe it with pratham├бс╕е (тАЬfirst among theseтАЭ) and supply тАЬcows.тАЭ But this doesnтАЩt make sense if the meaning is тАЬdesiring to run first among these,тАЭ because that conjures up a picture of the horse leading a stampede of cattle in a race – surely not an ancient Indian sporting event or battle array! If the ─Бsu is to be construed with the rest of its p─Бda, it should refer to the ranks of chariots in b (┼Ыr├йс╣Зibh─л r├бth─Бn─Бm): ┼Ыr├йс╣Зi- is fem.

and the image appears to be of Dadhikr─Б leading a charge of chariots, a far more likely scenario. However, I think unaccented ─Бsu is simply taking (modified) WackernagelтАЩs position in the clause and should be construed with n├н veveti in b: the horse is bearing down on the females. (Note that n├н veveti тАж ─Бsu is found also in III.55.9.) Even so, I would not supply тАШcowsтАЩ: although we are (too) accustomed to having (notional) cows as the goal of a hypermasculine animal in the ever-repeated formulae in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX, where Soma the bull seeks cows in the form of milk, in fact Dadhikr─Б should be seeking mares, not cows, if this is about his desire to mate.

However, if he is not seeking mates, but merely prizes, cows will do. (And note c├бrati g├│с╣гu g├бchan in 4b, where the cows are explicit.) The sexual reading I suggest for ab may be supported by p─Бda c, where I follow Grassmann, Renou, and Witzel Got┼Н (in n.) in taking j├бnya- as a member of a wedding party, not merely a man тАШbelonging to (oneтАЩs own) people, LandsmannтАЩ. For j├бnya- in a wedding context, see AV XI.8.1-2. Here the comparison is presumably between the garland of the winner of the race and that of a suitor or groomsman at a wedding.

Geldner and Renou (EVP 15.163) render kir├бс╣Зam as тАШreinтАЩ (Geldner Z├╝gel, Renou r├кne), flg.

S─Бyaс╣Зa. (─Бsyagataс╣Г khal─лnam), though Renou appears to recant in his n. Neither etymology nor the other occurrences of the word (not so tr. by Geldner, e.g.) support this interpr., and context also favors a version of тАШdustтАЩ (so Witzel Got┼Н тАШSt├дubchenтАЩ). Note kirate reс╣З├║m тАЬscatters dustтАЭ in 7d, where the verb kirate echoes kir├бс╣Зa-.

рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╕реНрдпрдГ рд╕рдГ рдЙрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рд╡реЗрдЬрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЧрдордирд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдорд░реНрдпреЗ рд╕рдорд░рдгреЗ рд╕рд╣реБрд░рд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣рдирд╢реАрд▓рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдореН рдЛрддрд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╡рдпрд╡реЗрди рдЦреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рддрдиреБрдВ рд╢реБрд╢реНрд░реВрд╖рдорд╛рдгрдГ рддреБрд░рдВ рдпрддреАрд╖реБ рддреНрд╡рд░рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреАрд╖реНрд╡рд╕реБрд░рд╕реЗрдирд╛рд╕реБ рддреБрд░рдпрдиреН рддреНрд╡рд░рдпрдиреН рдЛрдЬрд┐рдкреНрдпрдГ рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрд╛рдореА рд░реЗрдгреБрдВ рдзреВрд▓рд┐рдореН рдЛрдЮреНрдЬрдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдзрдпрдВрд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд░реЗрдгреБрдВ рднреНрд░реБрд╡реЛрдГ рдЕрдзрд┐ рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ рдХрд┐рд░рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкрддрд┐ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd that swift (horse) enduring in battle, bestowing food, and doing service with his limbs, rushing swiftly upon the quick-moving (host of the enemy), going straight onward, and tossing up the dust, throws it above his brows.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And this prizewinner, victorious, truthful, himself seeking fame with his own body in the clash,
hastening headlong toward them (fem. [=mares?]) as they go hastily, straight-flying, scatters dust up to the eyebrows as he stretches out
straight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On p─Бda b (=VII.19.2) see comm. on the latter passage. As discussed there, although the standard tr. (here Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) take ┼Ы├║┼Ыr┼лс╣гam─Бс╣Зaс╕е as a form of тИЪ┼Ыruс╣г тАШobeyтАЩ and tr. accordingly, it is simply a well-formed desiderative to тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhear / be heard/famedтАЩ (so classified by Grassmann, Wh [Rts], Heenen), with the mid. meaning тАШdesiring fame (for oneself), desiring to be(come) famedтАЩ. P─Бda c contains another unidentified fem. loc. pl., the pres. part. yat─л╠Бс╣гu. Oldenberg, Geldner, and Renou take the referent to be the ranks of chariots from 6b, Witzel Got┼Н cows. I again prefer mares (though the other two are possible, depending on how it is construed). I take the t├║ram, the acc. sg. of a root noun (see Schindler s.v., though I do not follow his interpr. of this passage), as an adverb. It forms a phrasal verb with тИЪi тАШgo hastilyтАЩ (so approx. Oldenberg). In context t├║raс╣Г ya(t─л╠Бс╣гu) is a close match to the immed. following tur├бyan. It would be an even better match if the 2nd participle were turaс╣Зy├бn (two forms of this verbal stem are found in the Dadhikr─Б hymn IV.40: turaс╣Зyat├бс╕е 3a, turaс╣Зyati 4a, and cf. also turaс╣Зyas├бt 2b), and I am tempted to think that the poet had this stem in mind, but opted for phonologically similar tur├бyant- because his preferred form would have produced a bad break. Like turaс╣Зyas├бt in 40.2, our form would be a deliberate deformation of the expected one to fit metrical circumstances, though our tur├бyan makes no morphological difficulties, unlike turaс╣Зyas├бt.

Griffith

And that strong Steed, victorious and faithful, obedient with his body in the combat,
Speeding straight on amid the swiftly ressing, casts o’er his brows the dust he tosses upward.

Geldner

Und dieser siegesgewohnte Preisrenner, der fromme, der mit seinem Leib in der Schlacht gehorcht, unter den wettlaufenden Wagenreihen vorausst├╝rmend, vorausschie├Яend wirft er Staub bis ├╝ber die Augenbrauen auf, an die Spitze eilend.

Grassmann

Es kommt dies Ross, das sieggewohnte, heil’ge, durch eigne Kraft bereit im Kampf zu helfen, Mit Eile dringend zu den raschen St├дmmen, erregend Staub, ihn sch├╝ttelnd von den Brauen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd the adversaries of that foe-destroying steed, like (those) of the brilliant thunderbolt, are alarmed; for when he contends, even against thousands on every side, then, rousing (his spirit), he is fearful and irresistible.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And they take fear at his charge as he shows his mettle, as if at the thundering of heaven.
When a thousand have battled him, the fearsome one becomes difficult to obstruct, as he stretches out straight.

Griffith

And at his thunder, like the roar of heaven, those who attack tremble and are affrighted;
For when he fights against embattled thousands, dread is he in his striving; none may stay him.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMen praise the overpowering rapidty of that fleet (steed), who is the accomplisher (of the desires) of mankind, and following him to battle, they have said, Dadhikr─Б with (his) thousands has gone forth against the foe.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And the peoples admire the speed of him who fills the territories, the superiority of the swift one.
And they say about him as they disperse at the encounter: тАЬDadhikr─Б has run away with thousands.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg points out, the contrastive lexemes s├бm тИЪi and v├н тИЪi are juxtaposed in samith├й viy├бntaс╕е.

Griffith

The people praise the overpowering swiftness of this fleet Steed who giveth men abundance.
Of him they say when drawing back from battle. Dadhikras hath sped forward with his thousands.

Geldner

Und die Leute preisen laut seine Schnelligkeit, die ├Ьberlegenheit des Renners, der alle L├дnder erf├╝llt. Und sie sagen von ihm, wenn sie auf dem Kampffeld auseinandergehen; Dadhikra ist mit Tausenden abgezogen.

Grassmann

Und seinen Lauf bewundern alle Menschen, die Uebermacht des schnellen Weltdurchdringers, Und von ihm sagen die im Kampfe fliehen: Dadhikra ist mit Tausenden entflohen.

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

рджрдзреАрдирд┐ рдХреНрд░рд╛рдорддреАрддрд┐ ‘рдЬрдирд╕рдирдЦрди’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЯреН, рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рджрд╛рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдИрджреГрд╢реЛ рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреАрд░реН рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЪрддреБрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреН рдирд┐рд╖рд╛рджрдкрдЮреНрдЪрдорд╛рдиреН рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рдЖрддрддрд╛рди рдЕрдиреНрдирд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди рдмрд▓рд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╡рддреАрдГ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд▓рд┐рдЯреН ред

рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ - рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдкрдГ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЖрддрддрд╛рди рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддреАрдЪрдХрд╛рд░ ред рдЕрдк рдПрд╡ рд╡рд╛ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рддрддрд╛рди ред ‘рдКрдбрд┐рджрдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрджреНрднреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд┐рд░реБрджрд╛рддреНрддрд╛ ред

рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ - рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рд╢реН рд╢рддрд╕рд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рдмрд╣реБрддрд░рд╕реНрдп рдмрд╣реБрддрдорд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд╛ рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рднрдХреНрддреЗрднреНрдпрд╕реНрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдВ рд╢рддрдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдиреЛрддрд┐ рджрджрд╛рддреАрддрд┐ ред рддреЗрдиреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЯреН, рддреЗрдиреИрд╡ рдЪрд╛рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдиреНрдирд╡рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╢реАрд▓рдГ ред рдЕрд░реНрддреЗрдГ ‘рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛрдкрд┐ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рдирд┐рдкреН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рднрд╛рдЧреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдЗрдорд╛ рдЗрдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛ рдордзреБрд╕рджреГрд╢реЗрди рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд░рд╕реЗрди рд╕рдореНрдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ рд╕рдВрд╕реГрдЬрддреБ ред рддрддреЛ рдордзреБрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рд╢реНрд░реЛрд╖реНрдпрддреАрддрд┐ рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреН рдХрд░реЛрддреБ ред рдЕрдпрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рднрд┐рд╢рдВрд╕рдирд╛рджрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрдореБрдЮреНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрдорд╣реЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDadhikr─Б has spread abroad the five classes of beings by his strength, as the sun (diffuses) the waters by his radiance; may he, the giver of hundreds and thousands, associate these praises with agreeable (rewards).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Dadhikr─Б has stretched over the five peoples with his vast power, like the sun over the waters with its light.
Gaining thousands, gaining hundreds, let the prizewinning steed infuse these words with honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich contains a three-termed simile / frame construction, in which all three terms are realized in both simile and frame. This is fairly unusual.

Renou nicely points out that the product of d would be what is later called the madhuparka, the concoction offered to an honored guest.

Griffith

Dadhikras hath o’erspread the Fivefold People with vigour, as the Sun lightens the waters.
May the strong Steed who winneth bundreds, thousands, requite with sweetness these my words and praises.

Keith

Dadhikra with his glory hath overspread the five peoples,
As the sun with his light the waters;
May the strong steed, winning a hundred, a thousand,
Fill with honey these words of ours.

Geldner

Dadhikra hat sich mit seiner Kraft ├╝ber die f├╝nf V├╢lker ausgedehnt wie der Sonnengott ├╝ber die Gew├дsser mit seinem Lichte. Der Tausendgewinner, Hundertgewinner, der sieghafte Renner soll diese Worte mit Honig durchtr├дnken.

Grassmann

Mit Kraft durchdrang Dadhikra alle V├╢lker, gleichwie die Sonne mit dem Licht die L├╝fte, Der schnelle Renner, hundert, tausend spendend, belohn mit dem, was s├╝ss ist, diese Spr├╝che.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдмрд▓ рд╕реЗ (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЗрд╡) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рджрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдкрдЮреНрдЪ) рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ (рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреАрдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рдЖ, рддрддрд╛рди) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдд рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рдГ) рд╣рдЬрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╢рддрд╕рд╛рдГ) рдФрд░ рд╕реИрдХреЬреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╡рд╛рдЬреА) рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдордзреНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рд╣рдд рд╢рд╣рдж рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рдЗрдорд╛) рдЗрди (рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд╡рдЪрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ (рд╕рдореН, рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ) рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░реЗ, рд╡рд╣реА рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИ ред рдЬреЛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдп рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рдЕрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдп рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгрдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрежрее рдпрд╣ рдЕреЬрддрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмрд╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЗрд╡ рджрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреА рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЛрд╜рдк рдЗрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╜рддрддрд╛рди рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рдГ рд╢рддрд╕рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рдордзреНрд╡реЗрдорд╛ рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рд╕рдореНрдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ рд╕ рдПрд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рджрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдпреЛ рджрдзрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдзрд░реНрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рдореНрдпрддреЗ рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ рд╕рдГ (рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдмрд▓реЗрди (рдкрдЮреНрдЪ) (рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреАрдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЗрд╡) рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреЗрд╡ (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рддрддрд╛рди) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдгреЛрддрд┐ (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рдГ) рдпрдГ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рдирддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬрддрд┐ рд╕рдГ (рд╢рддрд╕рд╛рдГ) рдпрдГ рд╢рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдирддрд┐ рд╕рдореНрднрдЬрддрд┐ (рд╡рд╛рдЬреА) рд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛) рдпрдГ рд╕рджреНрдпреЛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдиреН рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ (рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ) рд╕ рдмрдзреНрдирд╛рддреБ (рдордзреНрд╡рд╛) рдХреНрд╖реМрджреНрд░реЗрдг (рд╕рдореН) (рдЗрдорд╛) рдЗрдорд╛рдирд┐ (рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдЗрд╡ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрди рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдкрд╛рддрд┐ рд╕реЛрд╜рд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдиреНрджрдорд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрежрее рдЗрддреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдиреЗ рдкрд╛рдЪ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддреЛ рддреЛ рдЕрд╕реАрдо рдЖрдирдВрдж рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддреЛ. рее резреж рее
